  }\\n    \\n    return subtlex_dict\\n\\n# 2.2 Load SUBTLEX-US norms\\nsubtlex_dict = download_subtlex_us()\\n\\n# 2.3 Implement word frequency extraction with OOV handling\\nimport numpy as np\\nfrom collections import defaultdict\\n\\ndef extract_word_frequencies(sentence: str, freq_dict: dict, oov_strategy: str = 'log_minus_one') -> list:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract word frequencies for all words in a sentence.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        sentence: Input sentence\\n        freq_dict: Dictionary mapping words to frequency info\\n        oov_strategy: How to handle OOV words\\n            - 'log_minus_one': Use log(freq) = -1 (default SUBTLEX approach)\\n            - 'mean': Use mean frequency of in-vocabulary words\\n            - 'median': Use median frequency\\n            \\n    Returns:\\n        List of frequency values (log-transformed) for each word\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    import re\\n    words = re.findall(r\\\"\\\\b\\\\w+\\\\b\\\", sentence.lower())\\n    \\n    frequencies = []\\n    oov_count = 0\\n    \\n    for word in words:\\n        if word in freq_dict:\\n            # Use SUBTL_WF (frequency per million)\\n            freq = freq_dict[word]['subtlex_wf']\\n            # Log-transform (common practice for word frequencies)\\n            log_freq = np.log10(freq + 1)  # +1 to handle zero frequencies\\n            frequencies.append(log_freq)\\n        else:\\n            oov_count += 1\\n            if oov_strategy == 'log_minus_one':\\n                frequencies.append(-1)  # Conventional choice for OOV\\n            elif oov_strategy == 'mean':\\n                # Compute mean of in-vocabulary frequencies\\n                all_freqs = [np.log10(f['subtlex_wf'] + 1) for f in freq_dict.values()]\\n                frequencies.append(np.mean(all_freqs))\\n            elif oov_strategy == 'median':\\n                all_freqs = [np.log10(f['subtlex_wf'] + 1) for f in freq_dict.values()]\\n                frequencies.append(np.median(all_freqs))\\n    \\n    oov_rate = oov_count / len(words) if words else 0\\n    return frequencies, oov_rate\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 3: SYLLABLE COUNTING WITH CMU DICTIONARY\\n\\n```python\\n# 3.1 Implement CMUdict-based syllable counting\\nimport pronouncing\\nimport syllables as syllables_pkg  # Heuristic fallback\\n\\ndef count_syllables_cmudict(word: str) -> tuple:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Count syllables using CMU Pronouncing Dictionary.\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        (syllable_count, is_oov)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    phones = pronouncing.phones_for_word(word.lower())\\n    \\n    if phones:\\n        # Use first pronunciation\\n        count = pronouncing.syllable_count(phones[0])\\n        return count, False\\n    else:\\n        # OOV: use heuristic fallback\\n        count = syllables_pkg.estimate(word)\\n        return count, True\\n\\ndef extract_syllables(sentence: str) -> tuple:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract syllable counts for all words in a sentence.\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        (list of syllable counts, oov_rate)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    import re\\n    words = re.findall(r\\\"\\\\b\\\\w+\\\\b\\\", sentence.lower())\\n    \\n    syllable_counts = []\\n    oov_count = 0\\n    \\n    for word in words:\\n        count, is_oov = count_syllables_cmudict(word)\\n        syllable_counts.append(count)\\n        if is_oov:\\n            oov_count += 1\\n    \\n    oov_rate = oov_count / len(words) if words else 0\\n    return syllable_counts, oov_rate\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 4: FEATURE EXTRACTION\\n\\n```python\\n# 4.1 Extract all features for a sentence\\nimport numpy as np\\n\\ndef extract_sentence_features(sentence: str, subtlex_dict: dict) -> dict:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract all features for a sentence.\\n    \\n    Returns dictionary with:\\n        - Average features (traditional readability features)\\n        - Uniformity features (CV of word-level properties)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    import re\\n    words = re.findall(r\\\"\\\\b\\\\w+\\\\b\\\", sentence.lower())\\n    num_words = len(words)\\n    \\n    if num_words == 0:\\n        return None\\n    \\n    # Word lengths (in characters)\\n    word_lengths = [len(word) for word in words]\\n    \\n    # Syllable counts\\n    syllable_counts, syll_oov_rate = extract_syllables(sentence)\\n    \\n    # Word frequencies (log-transformed)\\n    word_freqs, freq_oov_rate = extract_word_frequencies(sentence, subtlex_dict)\\n    \\n    # ========== AVERAGE FEATURES (Traditional) ==========\\n    avg_word_length = np.mean(word_lengths)\\n    avg_syllables = np.mean(syllable_counts)\\n    avg_word_freq = np.mean(word_freqs)  # Note: already log-transformed\\n    \\n    # Additional traditional features\\n    sentence_length = num_words\\n    avg_word_length_chars = avg_word_length\\n    \\n    # ========== UNIFORMITY FEATURES (CV) ==========\\n    # Coefficient of Variation = std / mean\\n    # Handle edge cases (zero mean)\\n    \\n    def compute_cv(values):\\n        \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute coefficient of variation.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n        values = np.array(values)\\n        mean_val = np.mean(values)\\n        if mean_val == 0:\\n            return 0  # or np.nan, but 0 is safer for model training\\n        return np.std(values) / mean_val\\n    \\n    cv_word_length = compute_cv(word_lengths)\\n    cv_syllables = compute_cv(syllable_counts)\\n    cv_word_freq = compute_cv(word_freqs)\\n    \\n    # ========== COMPILE FEATURE DICTIONARY ==========\\n    features = {\\n        # Average (traditional) features\\n        'avg_word_length': avg_word_length,\\n        'avg_syllables': avg_syllables,\\n        'avg_word_freq': avg_word_freq,\\n        'sentence_length': sentence_length,\\n        \\n        # Uniformity features (CV)\\n        'cv_word_length': cv_word_length,\\n        'cv_syllables': cv_syllables,\\n        'cv_word_freq': cv_word_freq,\\n        \\n        # OOV rates (for analysis)\\n        'syll_oov_rate': syll_oov_rate,\\n        'freq_oov_rate': freq_oov_rate\\n    }\\n    \\n    return features\\n\\n# 4.2 Extract features for all sentences in dataset\\ndef extract_dataset_features(sentences: list, subtlex_dict: dict) -> tuple:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract features for all sentences in a dataset.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    all_features = []\\n    skipped = 0\\n    \\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        feats = extract_sentence_features(sent, subtlex_dict)\\n        if feats is not None:\\n            all_features.append(feats)\\n        else:\\n            skipped += 1\\n    \\n    if skipped > 0:\\n        print(f\\\"Skipped {skipped} sentences with no words\\\")\\n    \\n    # Convert to feature matrix\\n    feature_names = list(all_features[0].keys())\\n    # Remove OOV rates from model features (they're metadata)\\n    model_feature_names = [f for f in feature_names if not f.endswith('_oov_rate')]\\n    \\n    X = np.array([[f[name] for name in model_feature_names] for f in all_features])\\n    \\n    return X, model_feature_names, all_features\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 5: BERT-BASED BASELINE IMPLEMENTATION\\n\\n```python\\n# 5.1 Implement BERT-based readability model\\nimport torch\\nfrom transformers import BertModel, BertTokenizer, BertConfig\\nfrom torch import nn\\nfrom torch.utils.data import Dataset, DataLoader\\nfrom sklearn.model_selection import KFold\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import r2_score, mean_absolute_error\\nimport numpy as np\\n\\nclass ReadabilityBERTDataset(Dataset):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Dataset for BERT-based readability prediction.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    def __init__(self, sentences, scores, tokenizer, max_length=128):\\n        self.sentences = sentences\\n        self.scores = scores\\n        self.tokenizer = tokenizer\\n        self.max_length = max_length\\n    \\n    def __len__(self):\\n        return len(self.sentences)\\n    \\n    def __getitem__(self, idx):\\n        sentence = self.sentences[idx]\\n        score = self.scores[idx]\\n        \\n        # Tokenize\\n        encoding = self.tokenizer(\\n            sentence,\\n            truncation=True,\\n            padding='max_length',\\n            max_length=self.max_length,\\n            return_tensors='pt'\\n        )\\n        \\n        return {\\n            'input_ids': encoding['input_ids'].flatten(),\\n            'attention_mask': encoding['attention_mask'].flatten(),\\n            'labels': torch.tensor(score, dtype=torch.float)\\n        }\\n\\nclass BERTReadabilityModel(nn.Module):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"BERT model for readability prediction.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    def __init__(self, bert_model_name='bert-base-uncased', dropout=0.1):\\n        super().__init__()\\n        self.bert = BertModel.from_pretrained(bert_model_name)\\n        self.dropout = nn.Dropout(dropout)\\n        self.regressor = nn.Linear(self.bert.config.hidden_size, 1)\\n    \\n    def forward(self, input_ids, attention_mask):\\n        outputs = self.bert(input_ids=input_ids, attention_mask=attention_mask)\\n        \\n        # Mean-pool token embeddings (exclude [CLS] and [SEP]?)\\n        # Use [CLS] token representation\\n        pooled_output = outputs.last_hidden_state[:, 0, :]  # [CLS] token\\n        \\n        # Alternative: mean pooling\\n        # mask = attention_mask.unsqueeze(-1).expand(outputs.last_hidden_state.size())\\n        # pooled_output = (outputs.last_hidden_state * mask).sum(1) / mask.sum(1)\\n        \\n        pooled_output = self.dropout(pooled_output)\\n        logits = self.regressor(pooled_output)\\n        return logits.squeeze(-1)\\n\\ndef train_bert_model(train_loader, val_loader, device, num_epochs=3, learning_rate=2e-5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Train BERT model for readability prediction.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    model = BERTReadabilityModel()\\n    model.to(device)\\n    \\n    optimizer = torch.optim.AdamW(model.parameters(), lr=learning_rate)\\n    criterion = nn.MSELoss()\\n    \\n    for epoch in range(num_epochs):\\n        # Training\\n        model.train()\\n        train_loss = 0\\n        for batch in train_loader:\\n            input_ids = batch['input_ids'].to(device)\\n            attention_mask = batch['attention_mask'].to(device)\\n            labels = batch['labels'].to(device)\\n            \\n            optimizer.zero_grad()\\n            outputs = model(input_ids, attention_mask)\\n            loss = criterion(outputs, labels)\\n            loss.backward()\\n            torch.nn.utils.clip_grad_norm_(model.parameters(), 1.0)\\n            optimizer.step()\\n            \\n            train_loss += loss.item()\\n        \\n        # Validation\\n        model.eval()\\n        val_loss = 0\\n        val_preds = []\\n        val_labels = []\\n        with torch.no_grad():\\n            for batch in val_loader:\\n                input_ids = batch['input_ids'].to(device)\\n                attention_mask = batch['attention_mask'].to(device)\\n                labels = batch['labels'].to(device)\\n                \\n                outputs = model(input_ids, attention_mask)\\n                loss = criterion(outputs, labels)\\n                val_loss += loss.item()\\n                \\n                val_preds.extend(outputs.cpu().numpy())\\n                val_labels.extend(labels.cpu().numpy())\\n        \\n        val_r2 = r2_score(val_labels, val_preds)\\n        print(f\\\"Epoch {epoch+1}: Train Loss = {train_loss/len(train_loader):.4f}, \\\"\\n              f\\\"Val Loss = {val_loss/len(val_loader):.4f}, Val R\u00b2 = {val_r2:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    return model\\n\\ndef evaluate_bert_cv(sentences, scores, n_folds=5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Evaluate BERT model with n-fold cross-validation.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    device = torch.device('cuda' if torch.cuda.is_available() else 'cpu')\\n    tokenizer = BertTokenizer.from_pretrained('bert-base-uncased')\\n    \\n    kf = KFold(n_splits=n_folds, shuffle=True, random_state=42)\\n    \\n    all_preds = []\\n    all_labels = []\\n    fold_scores = []\\n    \\n    for fold, (train_idx, val_idx) in enumerate(kf.split(sentences)):\\n        print(f\\\"\\\\n=== Fold {fold+1}/{n_folds} ===\\\")\\n        \\n        # Split data\\n        train_sents = [sentences[i] for i in train_idx]\\n        train_scores = [scores[i] for i in train_idx]\\n        val_sents = [sentences[i] for i in val_idx]\\n        val_scores = [scores[i] for i in val_idx]\\n        \\n        # Create datasets\\n        train_dataset = ReadabilityBERTDataset(train_sents, train_scores, tokenizer)\\n        val_dataset = ReadabilityBERTDataset(val_sents, val_scores, tokenizer)\\n        \\n        train_loader = DataLoader(train_dataset, batch_size=16, shuffle=True)\\n        val_loader = DataLoader(val_dataset, batch_size=16)\\n        \\n        # Train model\\n        model = train_bert_model(train_loader, val_loader, device)\\n        \\n        # Evaluate\\n        model.eval()\\n        fold_preds = []\\n        with torch.no_grad():\\n            for batch in val_loader:\\n                input_ids = batch['input_ids'].to(device)\\n                attention_mask = batch['attention_mask'].to(device)\\n                outputs = model(input_ids, attention_mask)\\n                fold_preds.extend(outputs.cpu().numpy())\\n        \\n        fold_r2 = r2_score(val_scores, fold_preds)\\n        fold_scores.append(fold_r2)\\n        \\n        all_preds.extend(fold_preds)\\n        all_labels.extend(val_scores)\\n        \\n        print(f\\\"Fold {fold+1} R\u00b2 = {fold_r2:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    mean_r2 = np.mean(fold_scores)\\n    std_r2 = np.std(fold_scores)\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\nBERT CV R\u00b2: {mean_r2:.4f} \u00b1 {std_r2:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    return all_preds, all_labels, mean_r2, std_r2\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 6: LINEAR MODEL EVALUATION WITH BOOTSTRAP CIs\\n\\n```python\\n# 6.1 Implement evaluation with bootstrap confidence intervals\\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import LinearRegression, Ridge\\nfrom sklearn.model_selection import cross_val_predict, KFold\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import r2_score, mean_absolute_error\\nimport numpy as np\\nfrom typing import List, Dict, Tuple\\n\\ndef compute_bootstrap_ci(y_true: np.ndarray, y_pred1: np.ndarray, y_pred2: np.ndarray, \\n                         n_bootstrap: int = 10000, confidence_level: float = 0.95) -> Dict:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute bootstrap confidence interval for R\u00b2 difference between two models.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        y_true: True labels\\n        y_pred1: Predictions from model 1\\n        y_pred2: Predictions from model 2\\n        n_bootstrap: Number of bootstrap samples\\n        confidence_level: Confidence level for CI\\n        \\n    Returns:\\n        Dictionary with mean difference, std, CI bounds, p-value\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    n = len(y_true)\\n    \\n    # Compute R\u00b2 for original sample\\n    r2_1 = r2_score(y_true, y_pred1)\\n    r2_2 = r2_score(y_true, y_pred2)\\n    original_diff = r2_2 - r2_1\\n    \\n    # Bootstrap\\n    bootstrap_diffs = []\\n    rng = np.random.RandomState(42)\\n    \\n    for i in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        # Sample with replacement\\n        indices = rng.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        y_true_boot = y_true[indices]\\n        y_pred1_boot = y_pred1[indices]\\n        y_pred2_boot = y_pred2[indices]\\n        \\n        # Compute R\u00b2 for bootstrap sample\\n        r2_1_boot = r2_score(y_true_boot, y_pred1_boot)\\n        r2_2_boot = r2_score(y_true_boot, y_pred2_boot)\\n        bootstrap_diffs.append(r2_2_boot - r2_1_boot)\\n    \\n    bootstrap_diffs = np.array(bootstrap_diffs)\\n    \\n    # Compute statistics\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(bootstrap_diffs)\\n    std_diff = np.std(bootstrap_diffs)\\n    \\n    # Confidence interval\\n    alpha = 1 - confidence_level\\n    lower_percentile = (alpha / 2) * 100\\n    upper_percentile = (1 - alpha / 2) * 100\\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(bootstrap_diffs, lower_percentile)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(bootstrap_diffs, upper_percentile)\\n    \\n    # P-value (proportion of bootstrap samples where difference <= 0)\\n    p_value = np.mean(bootstrap_diffs <= 0)\\n    # Two-sided p-value\\n    p_value_two_sided = 2 * min(p_value, 1 - p_value)\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'r2_model1': r2_1,\\n        'r2_model2': r2_2,\\n        'difference': original_diff,\\n        'bootstrap_mean': mean_diff,\\n        'bootstrap_std': std_diff,\\n        'ci_lower': ci_lower,\\n        'ci_upper': ci_upper,\\n        'p_value': p_value_two_sided,\\n        'significant': ci_lower > 0 or ci_upper < 0\\n    }\\n\\ndef evaluate_feature_sets(X: np.ndarray, y: np.ndarray, feature_names: List[str], \\n                         n_folds: int = 5, n_bootstrap: int = 10000) -> Dict:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Evaluate different feature sets and compute bootstrap CIs for R\u00b2 differences.\\n    \\n    Feature sets to evaluate:\\n    1. Average features only (traditional)\\n    2. Uniformity features only (CV)\\n    3. Combined features (average + uniformity)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Identify feature indices\\n    avg_feature_indices = [i for i, name in enumerate(feature_names) \\n                          if name.startswith('avg_') or name == 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_feature_indices = [i for i, name in enumerate(feature_names) \\n                                  if name.startswith('cv_')]\\n    \\n    # Create feature matrices for each set\\n    X_avg = X[:, avg_feature_indices]\\n    X_uniform = X[:, uniformity_feature_indices]\\n    X_combined = X  # All features\\n    \\n    # Cross-validation setup\\n    kf = KFold(n_splits=n_folds, shuffle=True, random_state=42)\\n    \\n    results = {}\\n    \\n    # Evaluate each feature set\\n    for set_name, X_set in [('average', X_avg), ('uniformity', X_uniform), ('combined', X_combined)]:\\n        # Cross-validated predictions\\n        model = Ridge(alpha=1.0)  # Ridge regression for stability\\n        y_pred_cv = cross_val_predict(model, X_set, y, cv=kf)\\n        \\n        # Metrics\\n        r2 = r2_score(y, y_pred_cv)\\n        mae = mean_absolute_error(y, y_pred_cv)\\n        \\n        results[set_name] = {\\n            'predictions': y_pred_cv,\\n            'r2': r2,\\n            'mae': mae\\n        }\\n        \\n        print(f\\\"{set_name.capitalize()} features: R\u00b2 = {r2:.4f}, MAE = {mae:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    # Compute bootstrap CIs for R\u00b2 differences\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n=== Bootstrap Confidence Intervals for R\u00b2 Differences ===\\\")\\n    \\n    comparisons = [\\n        ('average', 'combined'),  # Does adding uniformity help?\\n        ('uniformity', 'combined'),  # Does adding average help?\\n        ('average', 'uniformity')  # Which is better alone?\\n    ]\\n    \\n    bootstrap_results = {}\\n    \\n    for name1, name2 in comparisons:\\n        comparison_name = f\\\"{name1}_vs_{name2}\\\"\\n        print(f\\\"\\\\nComparing {name1} vs {name2}:\\\")\\n        \\n        ci_result = compute_bootstrap_ci(\\n            y, \\n            results[name1]['predictions'], \\n            results[name2]['predictions'],\\n            n_bootstrap=n_bootstrap\\n        )\\n        \\n        bootstrap_results[comparison_name] = ci_result\\n        \\n        print(f\\\"  R\u00b2 ({name1}): {ci_result['r2_model1']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  R\u00b2 ({name2}): {ci_result['r2_model2']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Difference: {ci_result['difference']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Bootstrap mean diff: {ci_result['bootstrap_mean']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Bootstrap std diff: {ci_result['bootstrap_std']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  95% CI: [{ci_result['ci_lower']:.4f}, {ci_result['ci_upper']:.4f}]\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  P-value: {ci_result['p_value']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Significant: {ci_result['significant']}\\\")\\n    \\n    results['bootstrap_comparisons'] = bootstrap_results\\n    return results\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 7: COMPREHENSIVE EVALUATION\\n\\n```python\\n# 7.1 Run complete evaluation on both datasets\\nimport json\\nfrom pathlib import Path\\n\\ndef run_complete_evaluation():\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Run complete evaluation with all components.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    # Load datasets\\n    dataset_path = Path('/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_nOuUUSNqdMp4/3_invention_loop/iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_dataset_1/full_data_out.json')\\n    with open(dataset_path) as f:\\n        standardized_data = json.load(f)\\n    \\n    weebit_examples = standardized_data['datasets'][0]['examples']\\n    cefr_examples = standardized_data['datasets'][1]['examples']\\n    \\n    X_weebit_text = [ex['input'] for ex in weebit_examples]\\n    y_weebit = np.array([float(ex['output']) for ex in weebit_examples])\\n    \\n    X_cefr_text = [ex['input'] for ex in cefr_examples]\\n    y_cefr = np.array([float(ex['output']) for ex in cefr_examples])\\n    \\n    # Load SUBTLEX-US\\n    subtlex_dict = download_subtlex_us()\\n    \\n    # Extract features\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n=== Extracting features for WeeBIT ===\\\")\\n    X_weebit, feature_names, raw_features_weebit = extract_dataset_features(X_weebit_text, subtlex_dict)\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\n=== Extracting features for CEFR-SP ===\\\")\\n    X_cefr, feature_names, raw_features_cefr = extract_dataset_features(X_cefr_text, subtlex_dict)\\n    \\n    # Evaluate linear models with bootstrap CIs\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    print(\\\"EVALUATION ON WEEBIT\\\")\\n    print(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    results_weebit = evaluate_feature_sets(X_weebit, y_weebit, feature_names, n_folds=5, n_bootstrap=10000)\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    print(\\\"EVALUATION ON CEFR-SP\\\")\\n    print(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    results_cefr = evaluate_feature_sets(X_cefr, y_cefr, feature_names, n_folds=5, n_bootstrap=10000)\\n    \\n    # Evaluate BERT baseline\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    print(\\\"BERT BASELINE EVALUATION\\\")\\n    print(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\nBERT on WeeBIT:\\\")\\n    bert_preds_weebit, bert_labels_weebit, bert_r2_weebit, bert_std_weebit = evaluate_bert_cv(\\n        X_weebit_text, y_weebit, n_folds=5\\n    )\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\nBERT on CEFR-SP:\\\")\\n    bert_preds_cefr, bert_labels_cefr, bert_r2_cefr, bert_std_cefr = evaluate_bert_cv(\\n        X_cefr_text, y_cefr, n_folds=5\\n    )\\n    \\n    # Compile results\\n    final_results = {\\n        'weebit': {\\n            'n_samples': len(y_weebit),\\n            'linear_models': results_weebit,\\n            'bert': {\\n                'r2_mean': bert_r2_weebit,\\n                'r2_std': bert_std_weebit\\n            }\\n        },\\n        'cefr_sp': {\\n            'n_samples': len(y_cefr),\\n            'linear_models': results_cefr,\\n            'bert': {\\n                'r2_mean': bert_r2_cefr,\\n                'r2_std': bert_std_cefr\\n            }\\n        },\\n        'feature_names': feature_names,\\n        'subtlex_oov_rate': compute_oov_rate(X_weebit_text + X_cefr_text, subtlex_dict),\\n        'cmudict_oov_rate': compute_oov_rate_syllables(X_weebit_text + X_cefr_text)\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Save results\\n    with open('method_out.json', 'w') as f:\\n        json.dump(final_results, f, indent=2)\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    print(\\\"FINAL SUMMARY\\\")\\n    print(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    print(f\\\"WeeBIT: Linear (combined) R\u00b2 = {results_weebit['combined']['r2']:.4f}\\\")\\n    print(f\\\"         BERT R\u00b2 = {bert_r2_weebit:.4f}\\\")\\n    print(f\\\"CEFR-SP: Linear (combined) R\u00b2 = {results_cefr['combined']['r2']:.4f}\\\")\\n    print(f\\\"          BERT R\u00b2 = {bert_r2_cefr:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    return final_results\\n\\ndef compute_oov_rate(sentences: List[str], freq_dict: dict) -> float:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute overall OOV rate for word frequency dictionary.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    total_words = 0\\n    total_oov = 0\\n    \\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        words = re.findall(r\\\"\\\\b\\\\w+\\\\b\\\", sent.lower())\\n        total_words += len(words)\\n        for word in words:\\n            if word not in freq_dict:\\n                total_oov += 1\\n    \\n    return total_oov / total_words if total_words > 0 else 0\\n\\ndef compute_oov_rate_syllables(sentences: List[str]) -> float:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute OOV rate for CMUdict syllable counting.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    total_words = 0\\n    total_oov = 0\\n    \\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        words = re.findall(r\\\"\\\\b\\\\w+\\\\b\\\", sent.lower())\\n        total_words += len(words)\\n        for word in words:\\n            phones = pronouncing.phones_for_word(word)\\n            if not phones:\\n                total_oov += 1\\n    \\n    return total_oov / total_words if total_words > 0 else 0\\n\\n# 7.2 Execute evaluation\\nif __name__ == '__main__':\\n    results = run_complete_evaluation()\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 8: RESULTS ANALYSIS AND VISUALIZATION\\n\\n```python\\n# 8.1 Analyze and visualize results\\nimport matplotlib.pyplot as plt\\nimport seaborn as sns\\n\\ndef analyze_and_visualize(results: dict):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Analyze results and create visualizations.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    # 1. Compare R\u00b2 across models and datasets\\n    fig, axes = plt.subplots(2, 2, figsize=(12, 10))\\n    \\n    datasets = ['weebit', 'cefr_sp']\\n    model_names = ['average', 'uniformity', 'combined']\\n    \\n    for i, dataset in enumerate(datasets):\\n        ax = axes[i, 0]\\n        \\n        r2_values = [results[dataset]['linear_models'][name]['r2'] for name in model_names]\\n        ax.bar(model_names, r2_values)\\n        ax.set_title(f\\\"{dataset.upper()}: Linear Models R\u00b2\\\")\\n        ax.set_ylabel(\\\"R\u00b2\\\")\\n        ax.set_ylim([0, max(r2_values) * 1.2])\\n        \\n        # Add BERT R\u00b2\\n        ax.axhline(y=results[dataset]['bert']['r2_mean'], color='r', linestyle='--', \\n                   label=f\\\"BERT (R\u00b2={results[dataset]['bert']['r2_mean']:.3f})\\\")\\n        ax.legend()\\n    \\n    # 2. Visualize bootstrap distributions\\n    for i, dataset in enumerate(datasets):\\n        ax = axes[i, 1]\\n        \\n        bootstrap_data = results[dataset]['linear_models']['bootstrap_comparisons']\\n        \\n        # Example: visualize average vs combined difference\\n        diffs = bootstrap_data['average_vs_combined']['bootstrap_diffs']  # Would need to store these\\n        \\n        ax.hist(diffs, bins=50, edgecolor='black')\\n        ax.axvline(x=0, color='r', linestyle='--', label='No difference')\\n        ax.set_title(f\\\"{dataset.upper()}: Bootstrap Distribution\\\\n(Average vs Combined R\u00b2 Difference)\\\")\\n        ax.set_xlabel(\\\"R\u00b2 Difference\\\")\\n        ax.set_ylabel(\\\"Frequency\\\")\\n        ax.legend()\\n    \\n    plt.tight_layout()\\n    plt.savefig('results_visualization.png', dpi=300, bbox_inches='tight')\\n    \\n    # 3. Print detailed results table\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*80)\\n    print(\\\"DETAILED RESULTS TABLE\\\")\\n    print(\\\"=\\\"*80)\\n    \\n    header = f\\\"{'Model':<20} {'WeeBIT R\u00b2':<15} {'CEFR-SP R\u00b2':<15} {'BERT (both)':<15}\\\"\\n    print(header)\\n    print(\\\"-\\\" * 80)\\n    \\n    for model_name in model_names:\\n        weebit_r2 = results['weebit']['linear_models'][model_name]['r2']\\n        cefr_r2 = results['cefr_sp']['linear_models'][model_name]['r2']\\n        bert_r2 = results['weebit']['bert']['r2_mean']  # Same BERT for both\\n        print(f\\\"{model_name:<20} {weebit_r2:<15.4f} {cefr_r2:<15.4f} {bert_r2:<15.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\nBootstrap CI for R\u00b2 improvement (Average -> Combined):\\\")\\n    for dataset in datasets:\\n        boot = results[dataset]['linear_models']['bootstrap_comparisons']['average_vs_combined']\\n        print(f\\\"  {dataset.upper()}: \u0394R\u00b2 = {boot['difference']:.4f}, \\\"\\n              f\\\"95% CI [{boot['ci_lower']:.4f}, {boot['ci_upper']:.4f}], \\\"\\n              f\\\"p = {boot['p_value']:.4f}\\\")\\n\\n# 8.2 Run analysis\\nanalyze_and_visualize(results)\\n```\",\n  \"fallback_plan\": \"## FALLBACK PLAN: If Primary Approach Fails\\n\\n### Fallback 1: SUBTLEX-US Download Issues\\n**Problem**: Cannot download SUBTLEX-US from Ghent University (server down, access restricted).\\n\\n**Fallback Solutions**:\\n1. **Use HuggingFace mirror**: Search for `sgramm/subtlex-us` or similar on HuggingFace Hub\\n   ```python\\n   from datasets import load_dataset\\n   subtlex_dataset = load_dataset('sgramm/subtlex-us', split='train')\\n   subtlex_dict = {row['word']: {'subtlex_wf': row['SUBTL_WF'], 'zipf': row['Zipf']} \\n                   for row in subtlex_dataset}\\n   ```\\n\\n2. **Use Google Books Ngrams**: Download from GitHub repository\\n   ```python\\n   # Use orgtre/google-books-ngram-frequency repository\\n   # Provides cleaned word frequency lists\\n   ```\\n\\n3. **Use NLTK Gutenberg + Brown corpus**: Lower quality but accessible\\n   ```python\\n   import nltk\\n   from nltk.corpus import gutenberg, brown\\n   \\n   # Combine frequencies from both corpora\\n   freq_dist = nltk.FreqDist()\\n   for word in gutenberg.words():\\n       freq_dist[word.lower()] += 1\\n   for word in brown.words():\\n       freq_dist[word.lower()] += 1\\n   ```\\n\\n4. **Generate synthetic frequency norms**: For testing only\\n   ```python\\n   # Assign frequencies based on word length (approximation)\\n   # Short words tend to be more frequent\\n   def approx_frequency(word):\\n       return 1_000_000 / (len(word) ** 2)  # Heuristic\\n   ```\\n\\n**Implementation**: Try SUBTLEX-US download first. If fails, try HuggingFace (Fallbacks 1.1). If all fail, use NLTK corpora (Fallback 1.3) and document the limitation.\\n\\n### Fallback 2: BERT GPU Memory Issues\\n**Problem**: BERT model too large for available GPU memory (especially for RTX A4500 20GB).\\n\\n**Fallback Solutions**:\\n1. **Use smaller BERT variant**: `bert-base-uncased` is 110M parameters, try:\\n   - `distilbert-base-uncased` (66M parameters, ~50% faster)\\n   - `albert-base-v2` (12M parameters, very memory efficient)\\n   - `mobilebert-uncased` (25M parameters)\\n\\n2. **Reduce batch size**: Lower from 16 to 8 or 4\\n   ```python\\n   train_loader = DataLoader(train_dataset, batch_size=4, shuffle=True)  # Reduce batch size\\n   ```\\n\\n3. **Use gradient accumulation**: Simulate larger batch size with smaller memory\\n   ```python\\n   accumulation_steps = 4\\n   optimizer.zero_grad()\\n   for i, batch in enumerate(train_loader):\\n       outputs = model(**batch)\\n       loss = outputs.loss / accumulation_steps  # Normalize\\n       loss.backward()\\n       if (i + 1) % accumulation_steps == 0:\\n           optimizer.step()\\n           optimizer.zero_grad()\\n   ```\\n\\n4. **Use CPU for BERT**: Much slower but will complete\\n   ```python\\n   device = torch.device('cpu')  # Fallback to CPU\\n   ```\\n\\n5. **Skip BERT baseline**: If all else fails, compare only linear models\\n   ```python\\n   # Document that BERT baseline could not be computed due to resource constraints\\n   # Rely on literature comparison with reported BERT performance\\n   ```\\n\\n**Implementation**: Monitor GPU memory. If OOM, switch to distilbert (Fallback 2.1). If still OOM, reduce batch size (Fallback 2.2). Document all fallbacks.\\n\\n### Fallback 3: Bootstrap Too Slow\\n**Problem**: 10,000 bootstrap samples takes too long (> 2 hours).\\n\\n**Fallback Solutions**:\\n1. **Reduce bootstrap samples**: Use 1,000 or 2,000 samples\\n   ```python\\n   n_bootstrap = 2000  # Reduce from 10,000\\n   ```\\n\\n2. **Parallelize bootstrap computation**: Use multiprocessing\\n   ```python\\n   from multiprocessing import Pool\\n   import numpy as np\\n   \\n   def bootstrap_sample(args):\\n       y_true, y_pred1, y_pred2, rng_seed = args\\n       rng = np.random.RandomState(rng_seed)\\n       indices = rng.choice(len(y_true), size=len(y_true), replace=True)\\n       # Compute R\u00b2 difference for this sample\\n       return r2_score(y_true[indices], y_pred2[indices]) - r2_score(y_true[indices], y_pred1[indices])\\n   \\n   with Pool(processes=8) as pool:\\n       args_list = [(y_true, y_pred1, y_pred2, seed) for seed in range(n_bootstrap)]\\n       bootstrap_diffs = pool.map(bootstrap_sample, args_list)\\n   ```\\n\\n3. **Use parametric bootstrap**: Assume normal errors\\n   ```python\\n   # Generate synthetic data from fitted model\\n   # Faster than non-parametric bootstrap\\n   ```\\n\\n4. **Use asymptotic approximation**: Normal approximation for R\u00b2 difference\\n   ```python\\n   # Use formula for variance of R\u00b2 difference\\n   # Less accurate but much faster\\n   ```\\n\\n**Implementation**: Start with 10,000 bootstrap samples. If > 30 minutes, reduce to 2,000 (Fallback 3.1). If still slow, parallelize (Fallback 3.2).\\n\\n### Fallback 4: CMUdict Syllable Counting Too Slow\\n**Problem**: CMUdict lookup for every word in every sentence is slow for 13,129 sentences.\\n\\n**Fallback Solutions**:\\n1. **Pre-cache CMUdict**: Load entire dictionary into memory at start\\n   ```python\\n   import pronouncing\\n   \\n   # Pre-cache all pronunciations\\n   CMUDICT_CACHE = {}\\n   def get_syllables_cached(word):\\n       if word not in CMUDICT_CACHE:\\n           phones = pronouncing.phones_for_word(word)\\n           if phones:\\n               CMUDICT_CACHE[word] = pronouncing.syllable_count(phones[0])\\n           else:\\n               CMUDICT_CACHE[word] = syllables_pkg.estimate(word)  # Fallback\\n       return CMUDICT_CACHE[word]\\n   ```\\n\\n2. **Use syllables package for all words**: Lower accuracy but much faster\\n   ```python\\n   import syllables\\n   syllable_counts = [syllables.estimate(word) for word in words]\\n   ```\\n\\n3. **Sample sentences for evaluation**: Run full evaluation on subset\\n   ```python\\n   # Use 50% sample for testing\\n   sampled_indices = np.random.choice(len(sentences), size=len(sentences)//2, replace=False)\\n   sentences_sampled = [sentences[i] for i in sampled_indices]\\n   ```\\n\\n**Implementation**: Implement caching (Fallback 4.1).   }\\n    \\n    return subtlex_dict\\n\\n# 2.2 Load SUBTLEX-US norms\\nsubtlex_dict = download_subtlex_us()\\n\\n# 2.3 Implement word frequency extraction with OOV handling\\nimport numpy as np\\nfrom collections import defaultdict\\n\\ndef extract_word_frequencies(sentence: str, freq_dict: dict, oov_strategy: str = 'log_minus_one') -> list:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract word frequencies for all words in a sentence.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        sentence: Input sentence\\n        freq_dict: Dictionary mapping words to frequency info\\n        oov_strategy: How to handle OOV words\\n            - 'log_minus_one': Use log(freq) = -1 (default SUBTLEX approach)\\n            - 'mean': Use mean frequency of in-vocabulary words\\n            - 'median': Use median frequency\\n            \\n    Returns:\\n        List of frequency values (log-transformed) for each word\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    import re\\n    words = re.findall(r\\\"\\\\b\\\\w+\\\\b\\\", sentence.lower())\\n    \\n    frequencies = []\\n    oov_count = 0\\n    \\n    for word in words:\\n        if word in freq_dict:\\n            # Use SUBTL_WF (frequency per million)\\n            freq = freq_dict[word]['subtlex_wf']\\n            # Log-transform (common practice for word frequencies)\\n            log_freq = np.log10(freq + 1)  # +1 to handle zero frequencies\\n            frequencies.append(log_freq)\\n        else:\\n            oov_count += 1\\n            if oov_strategy == 'log_minus_one':\\n                frequencies.append(-1)  # Conventional choice for OOV\\n            elif oov_strategy == 'mean':\\n                # Compute mean of in-vocabulary frequencies\\n                all_freqs = [np.log10(f['subtlex_wf'] + 1) for f in freq_dict.values()]\\n                frequencies.append(np.mean(all_freqs))\\n            elif oov_strategy == 'median':\\n                all_freqs = [np.log10(f['subtlex_wf'] + 1) for f in freq_dict.values()]\\n                frequencies.append(np.median(all_freqs))\\n    \\n    oov_rate = oov_count / len(words) if words else 0\\n    return frequencies, oov_rate\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 3: SYLLABLE COUNTING WITH CMU DICTIONARY\\n\\n```python\\n# 3.1 Implement CMUdict-based syllable counting\\nimport pronouncing\\nimport syllables as syllables_pkg  # Heuristic fallback\\n\\ndef count_syllables_cmudict(word: str) -> tuple:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Count syllables using CMU Pronouncing Dictionary.\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        (syllable_count, is_oov)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    phones = pronouncing.phones_for_word(word.lower())\\n    \\n    if phones:\\n        # Use first pronunciation\\n        count = pronouncing.syllable_count(phones[0])\\n        return count, False\\n    else:\\n        # OOV: use heuristic fallback\\n        count = syllables_pkg.estimate(word)\\n        return count, True\\n\\ndef extract_syllables(sentence: str) -> tuple:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract syllable counts for all words in a sentence.\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n        (list of syllable counts, oov_rate)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    import re\\n    words = re.findall(r\\\"\\\\b\\\\w+\\\\b\\\", sentence.lower())\\n    \\n    syllable_counts = []\\n    oov_count = 0\\n    \\n    for word in words:\\n        count, is_oov = count_syllables_cmudict(word)\\n        syllable_counts.append(count)\\n        if is_oov:\\n            oov_count += 1\\n    \\n    oov_rate = oov_count / len(words) if words else 0\\n    return syllable_counts, oov_rate\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 4: FEATURE EXTRACTION\\n\\n```python\\n# 4.1 Extract all features for a sentence\\nimport numpy as np\\n\\ndef extract_sentence_features(sentence: str, subtlex_dict: dict) -> dict:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract all features for a sentence.\\n    \\n    Returns dictionary with:\\n        - Average features (traditional readability features)\\n        - Uniformity features (CV of word-level properties)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    import re\\n    words = re.findall(r\\\"\\\\b\\\\w+\\\\b\\\", sentence.lower())\\n    num_words = len(words)\\n    \\n    if num_words == 0:\\n        return None\\n    \\n    # Word lengths (in characters)\\n    word_lengths = [len(word) for word in words]\\n    \\n    # Syllable counts\\n    syllable_counts, syll_oov_rate = extract_syllables(sentence)\\n    \\n    # Word frequencies (log-transformed)\\n    word_freqs, freq_oov_rate = extract_word_frequencies(sentence, subtlex_dict)\\n    \\n    # ========== AVERAGE FEATURES (Traditional) ==========\\n    avg_word_length = np.mean(word_lengths)\\n    avg_syllables = np.mean(syllable_counts)\\n    avg_word_freq = np.mean(word_freqs)  # Note: already log-transformed\\n    \\n    # Additional traditional features\\n    sentence_length = num_words\\n    avg_word_length_chars = avg_word_length\\n    \\n    # ========== UNIFORMITY FEATURES (CV) ==========\\n    # Coefficient of Variation = std / mean\\n    # Handle edge cases (zero mean)\\n    \\n    def compute_cv(values):\\n        \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute coefficient of variation.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n        values = np.array(values)\\n        mean_val = np.mean(values)\\n        if mean_val == 0:\\n            return 0  # or np.nan, but 0 is safer for model training\\n        return np.std(values) / mean_val\\n    \\n    cv_word_length = compute_cv(word_lengths)\\n    cv_syllables = compute_cv(syllable_counts)\\n    cv_word_freq = compute_cv(word_freqs)\\n    \\n    # ========== COMPILE FEATURE DICTIONARY ==========\\n    features = {\\n        # Average (traditional) features\\n        'avg_word_length': avg_word_length,\\n        'avg_syllables': avg_syllables,\\n        'avg_word_freq': avg_word_freq,\\n        'sentence_length': sentence_length,\\n        \\n        # Uniformity features (CV)\\n        'cv_word_length': cv_word_length,\\n        'cv_syllables': cv_syllables,\\n        'cv_word_freq': cv_word_freq,\\n        \\n        # OOV rates (for analysis)\\n        'syll_oov_rate': syll_oov_rate,\\n        'freq_oov_rate': freq_oov_rate\\n    }\\n    \\n    return features\\n\\n# 4.2 Extract features for all sentences in dataset\\ndef extract_dataset_features(sentences: list, subtlex_dict: dict) -> tuple:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract features for all sentences in a dataset.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    all_features = []\\n    skipped = 0\\n    \\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        feats = extract_sentence_features(sent, subtlex_dict)\\n        if feats is not None:\\n            all_features.append(feats)\\n        else:\\n            skipped += 1\\n    \\n    if skipped > 0:\\n        print(f\\\"Skipped {skipped} sentences with no words\\\")\\n    \\n    # Convert to feature matrix\\n    feature_names = list(all_features[0].keys())\\n    # Remove OOV rates from model features (they're metadata)\\n    model_feature_names = [f for f in feature_names if not f.endswith('_oov_rate')]\\n    \\n    X = np.array([[f[name] for name in model_feature_names] for f in all_features])\\n    \\n    return X, model_feature_names, all_features\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 5: BERT-BASED BASELINE IMPLEMENTATION\\n\\n```python\\n# 5.1 Implement BERT-based readability model\\nimport torch\\nfrom transformers import BertModel, BertTokenizer, BertConfig\\nfrom torch import nn\\nfrom torch.utils.data import Dataset, DataLoader\\nfrom sklearn.model_selection import KFold\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import r2_score, mean_absolute_error\\nimport numpy as np\\n\\nclass ReadabilityBERTDataset(Dataset):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Dataset for BERT-based readability prediction.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    def __init__(self, sentences, scores, tokenizer, max_length=128):\\n        self.sentences = sentences\\n        self.scores = scores\\n        self.tokenizer = tokenizer\\n        self.max_length = max_length\\n    \\n    def __len__(self):\\n        return len(self.sentences)\\n    \\n    def __getitem__(self, idx):\\n        sentence = self.sentences[idx]\\n        score = self.scores[idx]\\n        \\n        # Tokenize\\n        encoding = self.tokenizer(\\n            sentence,\\n            truncation=True,\\n            padding='max_length',\\n            max_length=self.max_length,\\n            return_tensors='pt'\\n        )\\n        \\n        return {\\n            'input_ids': encoding['input_ids'].flatten(),\\n            'attention_mask': encoding['attention_mask'].flatten(),\\n            'labels': torch.tensor(score, dtype=torch.float)\\n        }\\n\\nclass BERTReadabilityModel(nn.Module):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"BERT model for readability prediction.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    def __init__(self, bert_model_name='bert-base-uncased', dropout=0.1):\\n        super().__init__()\\n        self.bert = BertModel.from_pretrained(bert_model_name)\\n        self.dropout = nn.Dropout(dropout)\\n        self.regressor = nn.Linear(self.bert.config.hidden_size, 1)\\n    \\n    def forward(self, input_ids, attention_mask):\\n        outputs = self.bert(input_ids=input_ids, attention_mask=attention_mask)\\n        \\n        # Mean-pool token embeddings (exclude [CLS] and [SEP]?)\\n        # Use [CLS] token representation\\n        pooled_output = outputs.last_hidden_state[:, 0, :]  # [CLS] token\\n        \\n        # Alternative: mean pooling\\n        # mask = attention_mask.unsqueeze(-1).expand(outputs.last_hidden_state.size())\\n        # pooled_output = (outputs.last_hidden_state * mask).sum(1) / mask.sum(1)\\n        \\n        pooled_output = self.dropout(pooled_output)\\n        logits = self.regressor(pooled_output)\\n        return logits.squeeze(-1)\\n\\ndef train_bert_model(train_loader, val_loader, device, num_epochs=3, learning_rate=2e-5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Train BERT model for readability prediction.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    model = BERTReadabilityModel()\\n    model.to(device)\\n    \\n    optimizer = torch.optim.AdamW(model.parameters(), lr=learning_rate)\\n    criterion = nn.MSELoss()\\n    \\n    for epoch in range(num_epochs):\\n        # Training\\n        model.train()\\n        train_loss = 0\\n        for batch in train_loader:\\n            input_ids = batch['input_ids'].to(device)\\n            attention_mask = batch['attention_mask'].to(device)\\n            labels = batch['labels'].to(device)\\n            \\n            optimizer.zero_grad()\\n            outputs = model(input_ids, attention_mask)\\n            loss = criterion(outputs, labels)\\n            loss.backward()\\n            torch.nn.utils.clip_grad_norm_(model.parameters(), 1.0)\\n            optimizer.step()\\n            \\n            train_loss += loss.item()\\n        \\n        # Validation\\n        model.eval()\\n        val_loss = 0\\n        val_preds = []\\n        val_labels = []\\n        with torch.no_grad():\\n            for batch in val_loader:\\n                input_ids = batch['input_ids'].to(device)\\n                attention_mask = batch['attention_mask'].to(device)\\n                labels = batch['labels'].to(device)\\n                \\n                outputs = model(input_ids, attention_mask)\\n                loss = criterion(outputs, labels)\\n                val_loss += loss.item()\\n                \\n                val_preds.extend(outputs.cpu().numpy())\\n                val_labels.extend(labels.cpu().numpy())\\n        \\n        val_r2 = r2_score(val_labels, val_preds)\\n        print(f\\\"Epoch {epoch+1}: Train Loss = {train_loss/len(train_loader):.4f}, \\\"\\n              f\\\"Val Loss = {val_loss/len(val_loader):.4f}, Val R\u00b2 = {val_r2:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    return model\\n\\ndef evaluate_bert_cv(sentences, scores, n_folds=5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Evaluate BERT model with n-fold cross-validation.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    device = torch.device('cuda' if torch.cuda.is_available() else 'cpu')\\n    tokenizer = BertTokenizer.from_pretrained('bert-base-uncased')\\n    \\n    kf = KFold(n_splits=n_folds, shuffle=True, random_state=42)\\n    \\n    all_preds = []\\n    all_labels = []\\n    fold_scores = []\\n    \\n    for fold, (train_idx, val_idx) in enumerate(kf.split(sentences)):\\n        print(f\\\"\\\\n=== Fold {fold+1}/{n_folds} ===\\\")\\n        \\n        # Split data\\n        train_sents = [sentences[i] for i in train_idx]\\n        train_scores = [scores[i] for i in train_idx]\\n        val_sents = [sentences[i] for i in val_idx]\\n        val_scores = [scores[i] for i in val_idx]\\n        \\n        # Create datasets\\n        train_dataset = ReadabilityBERTDataset(train_sents, train_scores, tokenizer)\\n        val_dataset = ReadabilityBERTDataset(val_sents, val_scores, tokenizer)\\n        \\n        train_loader = DataLoader(train_dataset, batch_size=16, shuffle=True)\\n        val_loader = DataLoader(val_dataset, batch_size=16)\\n        \\n        # Train model\\n        model = train_bert_model(train_loader, val_loader, device)\\n        \\n        # Evaluate\\n        model.eval()\\n        fold_preds = []\\n        with torch.no_grad():\\n            for batch in val_loader:\\n                input_ids = batch['input_ids'].to(device)\\n                attention_mask = batch['attention_mask'].to(device)\\n                outputs = model(input_ids, attention_mask)\\n                fold_preds.extend(outputs.cpu().numpy())\\n        \\n        fold_r2 = r2_score(val_scores, fold_preds)\\n        fold_scores.append(fold_r2)\\n        \\n        all_preds.extend(fold_preds)\\n        all_labels.extend(val_scores)\\n        \\n        print(f\\\"Fold {fold+1} R\u00b2 = {fold_r2:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    mean_r2 = np.mean(fold_scores)\\n    std_r2 = np.std(fold_scores)\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\nBERT CV R\u00b2: {mean_r2:.4f} \u00b1 {std_r2:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    return all_preds, all_labels, mean_r2, std_r2\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 6: LINEAR MODEL EVALUATION WITH BOOTSTRAP CIs\\n\\n```python\\n# 6.1 Implement evaluation with bootstrap confidence intervals\\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import LinearRegression, Ridge\\nfrom sklearn.model_selection import cross_val_predict, KFold\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import r2_score, mean_absolute_error\\nimport numpy as np\\nfrom typing import List, Dict, Tuple\\n\\ndef compute_bootstrap_ci(y_true: np.ndarray, y_pred1: np.ndarray, y_pred2: np.ndarray, \\n                         n_bootstrap: int = 10000, confidence_level: float = 0.95) -> Dict:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute bootstrap confidence interval for R\u00b2 difference between two models.\\n    \\n    Args:\\n        y_true: True labels\\n        y_pred1: Predictions from model 1\\n        y_pred2: Predictions from model 2\\n        n_bootstrap: Number of bootstrap samples\\n        confidence_level: Confidence level for CI\\n        \\n    Returns:\\n        Dictionary with mean difference, std, CI bounds, p-value\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    n = len(y_true)\\n    \\n    # Compute R\u00b2 for original sample\\n    r2_1 = r2_score(y_true, y_pred1)\\n    r2_2 = r2_score(y_true, y_pred2)\\n    original_diff = r2_2 - r2_1\\n    \\n    # Bootstrap\\n    bootstrap_diffs = []\\n    rng = np.random.RandomState(42)\\n    \\n    for i in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        # Sample with replacement\\n        indices = rng.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        y_true_boot = y_true[indices]\\n        y_pred1_boot = y_pred1[indices]\\n        y_pred2_boot = y_pred2[indices]\\n        \\n        # Compute R\u00b2 for bootstrap sample\\n        r2_1_boot = r2_score(y_true_boot, y_pred1_boot)\\n        r2_2_boot = r2_score(y_true_boot, y_pred2_boot)\\n        bootstrap_diffs.append(r2_2_boot - r2_1_boot)\\n    \\n    bootstrap_diffs = np.array(bootstrap_diffs)\\n    \\n    # Compute statistics\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(bootstrap_diffs)\\n    std_diff = np.std(bootstrap_diffs)\\n    \\n    # Confidence interval\\n    alpha = 1 - confidence_level\\n    lower_percentile = (alpha / 2) * 100\\n    upper_percentile = (1 - alpha / 2) * 100\\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(bootstrap_diffs, lower_percentile)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(bootstrap_diffs, upper_percentile)\\n    \\n    # P-value (proportion of bootstrap samples where difference <= 0)\\n    p_value = np.mean(bootstrap_diffs <= 0)\\n    # Two-sided p-value\\n    p_value_two_sided = 2 * min(p_value, 1 - p_value)\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'r2_model1': r2_1,\\n        'r2_model2': r2_2,\\n        'difference': original_diff,\\n        'bootstrap_mean': mean_diff,\\n        'bootstrap_std': std_diff,\\n        'ci_lower': ci_lower,\\n        'ci_upper': ci_upper,\\n        'p_value': p_value_two_sided,\\n        'significant': ci_lower > 0 or ci_upper < 0\\n    }\\n\\ndef evaluate_feature_sets(X: np.ndarray, y: np.ndarray, feature_names: List[str], \\n                         n_folds: int = 5, n_bootstrap: int = 10000) -> Dict:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Evaluate different feature sets and compute bootstrap CIs for R\u00b2 differences.\\n    \\n    Feature sets to evaluate:\\n    1. Average features only (traditional)\\n    2. Uniformity features only (CV)\\n    3. Combined features (average + uniformity)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Identify feature indices\\n    avg_feature_indices = [i for i, name in enumerate(feature_names) \\n                          if name.startswith('avg_') or name == 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_feature_indices = [i for i, name in enumerate(feature_names) \\n                                  if name.startswith('cv_')]\\n    \\n    # Create feature matrices for each set\\n    X_avg = X[:, avg_feature_indices]\\n    X_uniform = X[:, uniformity_feature_indices]\\n    X_combined = X  # All features\\n    \\n    # Cross-validation setup\\n    kf = KFold(n_splits=n_folds, shuffle=True, random_state=42)\\n    \\n    results = {}\\n    \\n    # Evaluate each feature set\\n    for set_name, X_set in [('average', X_avg), ('uniformity', X_uniform), ('combined', X_combined)]:\\n        # Cross-validated predictions\\n        model = Ridge(alpha=1.0)  # Ridge regression for stability\\n        y_pred_cv = cross_val_predict(model, X_set, y, cv=kf)\\n        \\n        # Metrics\\n        r2 = r2_score(y, y_pred_cv)\\n        mae = mean_absolute_error(y, y_pred_cv)\\n        \\n        results[set_name] = {\\n            'predictions': y_pred_cv,\\n            'r2': r2,\\n            'mae': mae\\n        }\\n        \\n        print(f\\\"{set_name.capitalize()} features: R\u00b2 = {r2:.4f}, MAE = {mae:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    # Compute bootstrap CIs for R\u00b2 differences\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n=== Bootstrap Confidence Intervals for R\u00b2 Differences ===\\\")\\n    \\n    comparisons = [\\n        ('average', 'combined'),  # Does adding uniformity help?\\n        ('uniformity', 'combined'),  # Does adding average help?\\n        ('average', 'uniformity')  # Which is better alone?\\n    ]\\n    \\n    bootstrap_results = {}\\n    \\n    for name1, name2 in comparisons:\\n        comparison_name = f\\\"{name1}_vs_{name2}\\\"\\n        print(f\\\"\\\\nComparing {name1} vs {name2}:\\\")\\n        \\n        ci_result = compute_bootstrap_ci(\\n            y, \\n            results[name1]['predictions'], \\n            results[name2]['predictions'],\\n            n_bootstrap=n_bootstrap\\n        )\\n        \\n        bootstrap_results[comparison_name] = ci_result\\n        \\n        print(f\\\"  R\u00b2 ({name1}): {ci_result['r2_model1']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  R\u00b2 ({name2}): {ci_result['r2_model2']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Difference: {ci_result['difference']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Bootstrap mean diff: {ci_result['bootstrap_mean']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Bootstrap std diff: {ci_result['bootstrap_std']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  95% CI: [{ci_result['ci_lower']:.4f}, {ci_result['ci_upper']:.4f}]\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  P-value: {ci_result['p_value']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Significant: {ci_result['significant']}\\\")\\n    \\n    results['bootstrap_comparisons'] = bootstrap_results\\n    return results\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 7: COMPREHENSIVE EVALUATION\\n\\n```python\\n# 7.1 Run complete evaluation on both datasets\\nimport json\\nfrom pathlib import Path\\n\\ndef run_complete_evaluation():\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Run complete evaluation with all components.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    # Load datasets\\n    dataset_path = Path('/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_nOuUUSNqdMp4/3_invention_loop/iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_dataset_1/full_data_out.json')\\n    with open(dataset_path) as f:\\n        standardized_data = json.load(f)\\n    \\n    weebit_examples = standardized_data['datasets'][0]['examples']\\n    cefr_examples = standardized_data['datasets'][1]['examples']\\n    \\n    X_weebit_text = [ex['input'] for ex in weebit_examples]\\n    y_weebit = np.array([float(ex['output']) for ex in weebit_examples])\\n    \\n    X_cefr_text = [ex['input'] for ex in cefr_examples]\\n    y_cefr = np.array([float(ex['output']) for ex in cefr_examples])\\n    \\n    # Load SUBTLEX-US\\n    subtlex_dict = download_subtlex_us()\\n    \\n    # Extract features\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n=== Extracting features for WeeBIT ===\\\")\\n    X_weebit, feature_names, raw_features_weebit = extract_dataset_features(X_weebit_text, subtlex_dict)\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\n=== Extracting features for CEFR-SP ===\\\")\\n    X_cefr, feature_names, raw_features_cefr = extract_dataset_features(X_cefr_text, subtlex_dict)\\n    \\n    # Evaluate linear models with bootstrap CIs\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    print(\\\"EVALUATION ON WEEBIT\\\")\\n    print(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    results_weebit = evaluate_feature_sets(X_weebit, y_weebit, feature_names, n_folds=5, n_bootstrap=10000)\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    print(\\\"EVALUATION ON CEFR-SP\\\")\\n    print(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    results_cefr = evaluate_feature_sets(X_cefr, y_cefr, feature_names, n_folds=5, n_bootstrap=10000)\\n    \\n    # Evaluate BERT baseline\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    print(\\\"BERT BASELINE EVALUATION\\\")\\n    print(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\nBERT on WeeBIT:\\\")\\n    bert_preds_weebit, bert_labels_weebit, bert_r2_weebit, bert_std_weebit = evaluate_bert_cv(\\n        X_weebit_text, y_weebit, n_folds=5\\n    )\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\nBERT on CEFR-SP:\\\")\\n    bert_preds_cefr, bert_labels_cefr, bert_r2_cefr, bert_std_cefr = evaluate_bert_cv(\\n        X_cefr_text, y_cefr, n_folds=5\\n    )\\n    \\n    # Compile results\\n    final_results = {\\n        'weebit': {\\n            'n_samples': len(y_weebit),\\n            'linear_models': results_weebit,\\n            'bert': {\\n                'r2_mean': bert_r2_weebit,\\n                'r2_std': bert_std_weebit\\n            }\\n        },\\n        'cefr_sp': {\\n            'n_samples': len(y_cefr),\\n            'linear_models': results_cefr,\\n            'bert': {\\n                'r2_mean': bert_r2_cefr,\\n                'r2_std': bert_std_cefr\\n            }\\n        },\\n        'feature_names': feature_names,\\n        'subtlex_oov_rate': compute_oov_rate(X_weebit_text + X_cefr_text, subtlex_dict),\\n        'cmudict_oov_rate': compute_oov_rate_syllables(X_weebit_text + X_cefr_text)\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Save results\\n    with open('method_out.json', 'w') as f:\\n        json.dump(final_results, f, indent=2)\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    print(\\\"FINAL SUMMARY\\\")\\n    print(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\n    print(f\\\"WeeBIT: Linear (combined) R\u00b2 = {results_weebit['combined']['r2']:.4f}\\\")\\n    print(f\\\"         BERT R\u00b2 = {bert_r2_weebit:.4f}\\\")\\n    print(f\\\"CEFR-SP: Linear (combined) R\u00b2 = {results_cefr['combined']['r2']:.4f}\\\")\\n    print(f\\\"          BERT R\u00b2 = {bert_r2_cefr:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    return final_results\\n\\ndef compute_oov_rate(sentences: List[str], freq_dict: dict) -> float:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute overall OOV rate for word frequency dictionary.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    total_words = 0\\n    total_oov = 0\\n    \\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        words = re.findall(r\\\"\\\\b\\\\w+\\\\b\\\", sent.lower())\\n        total_words += len(words)\\n        for word in words:\\n            if word not in freq_dict:\\n                total_oov += 1\\n    \\n    return total_oov / total_words if total_words > 0 else 0\\n\\ndef compute_oov_rate_syllables(sentences: List[str]) -> float:\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute OOV rate for CMUdict syllable counting.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    total_words = 0\\n    total_oov = 0\\n    \\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        words = re.findall(r\\\"\\\\b\\\\w+\\\\b\\\", sent.lower())\\n        total_words += len(words)\\n        for word in words:\\n            phones = pronouncing.phones_for_word(word)\\n            if not phones:\\n                total_oov += 1\\n    \\n    return total_oov / total_words if total_words > 0 else 0\\n\\n# 7.2 Execute evaluation\\nif __name__ == '__main__':\\n    results = run_complete_evaluation()\\n```\\n\\n## PHASE 8: RESULTS ANALYSIS AND VISUALIZATION\\n\\n```python\\n# 8.1 Analyze and visualize results\\nimport matplotlib.pyplot as plt\\nimport seaborn as sns\\n\\ndef analyze_and_visualize(results: dict):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Analyze results and create visualizations.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    # 1. Compare R\u00b2 across models and datasets\\n    fig, axes = plt.subplots(2, 2, figsize=(12, 10))\\n    \\n    datasets = ['weebit', 'cefr_sp']\\n    model_names = ['average', 'uniformity', 'combined']\\n    \\n    for i, dataset in enumerate(datasets):\\n        ax = axes[i, 0]\\n        \\n        r2_values = [results[dataset]['linear_models'][name]['r2'] for name in model_names]\\n        ax.bar(model_names, r2_values)\\n        ax.set_title(f\\\"{dataset.upper()}: Linear Models R\u00b2\\\")\\n        ax.set_ylabel(\\\"R\u00b2\\\")\\n        ax.set_ylim([0, max(r2_values) * 1.2])\\n        \\n        # Add BERT R\u00b2\\n        ax.axhline(y=results[dataset]['bert']['r2_mean'], color='r', linestyle='--', \\n                   label=f\\\"BERT (R\u00b2={results[dataset]['bert']['r2_mean']:.3f})\\\")\\n        ax.legend()\\n    \\n    # 2. Visualize bootstrap distributions\\n    for i, dataset in enumerate(datasets):\\n        ax = axes[i, 1]\\n        \\n        bootstrap_data = results[dataset]['linear_models']['bootstrap_comparisons']\\n        \\n        # Example: visualize average vs combined difference\\n        diffs = bootstrap_data['average_vs_combined']['bootstrap_diffs']  # Would need to store these\\n        \\n        ax.hist(diffs, bins=50, edgecolor='black')\\n        ax.axvline(x=0, color='r', linestyle='--', label='No difference')\\n        ax.set_title(f\\\"{dataset.upper()}: Bootstrap Distribution\\\\n(Average vs Combined R\u00b2 Difference)\\\")\\n        ax.set_xlabel(\\\"R\u00b2 Difference\\\")\\n        ax.set_ylabel(\\\"Frequency\\\")\\n        ax.legend()\\n    \\n    plt.tight_layout()\\n    plt.savefig('results_visualization.png', dpi=300, bbox_inches='tight')\\n    \\n    # 3. Print detailed results table\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*80)\\n    print(\\\"DETAILED RESULTS TABLE\\\")\\n    print(\\\"=\\\"*80)\\n    \\n    header = f\\\"{'Model':<20} {'WeeBIT R\u00b2':<15} {'CEFR-SP R\u00b2':<15} {'BERT (both)':<15}\\\"\\n    print(header)\\n    print(\\\"-\\\" * 80)\\n    \\n    for model_name in model_names:\\n        weebit_r2 = results['weebit']['linear_models'][model_name]['r2']\\n        cefr_r2 = results['cefr_sp']['linear_models'][model_name]['r2']\\n        bert_r2 = results['weebit']['bert']['r2_mean']  # Same BERT for both\\n        print(f\\\"{model_name:<20} {weebit_r2:<15.4f} {cefr_r2:<15.4f} {bert_r2:<15.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\nBootstrap CI for R\u00b2 improvement (Average -> Combined):\\\")\\n    for dataset in datasets:\\n        boot = results[dataset]['linear_models']['bootstrap_comparisons']['average_vs_combined']\\n        print(f\\\"  {dataset.upper()}: \u0394R\u00b2 = {boot['difference']:.4f}, \\\"\\n              f\\\"95% CI [{boot['ci_lower']:.4f}, {boot['ci_upper']:.4f}], \\\"\\n              f\\\"p = {boot['p_value']:.4f}\\\")\\n\\n# 8.2 Run analysis\\nanalyze_and_visualize(results)\\n```\",\n  \"fallback_plan\": \"## FALLBACK PLAN: If Primary Approach Fails\\n\\n### Fallback 1: SUBTLEX-US Download Issues\\n**Problem**: Cannot download SUBTLEX-US from Ghent University (server down, access restricted).\\n\\n**Fallback Solutions**:\\n1. **Use HuggingFace mirror**: Search for `sgramm/subtlex-us` or similar on HuggingFace Hub\\n   ```python\\n   from datasets import load_dataset\\n   subtlex_dataset = load_dataset('sgramm/subtlex-us', split='train')\\n   subtlex_dict = {row['word']: {'subtlex_wf': row['SUBTL_WF'], 'zipf': row['Zipf']} \\n                   for row in subtlex_dataset}\\n   ```\\n\\n2. **Use Google Books Ngrams**: Download from GitHub repository\\n   ```python\\n   # Use orgtre/google-books-ngram-frequency repository\\n   # Provides cleaned word frequency lists\\n   ```\\n\\n3. **Use NLTK Gutenberg + Brown corpus**: Lower quality but accessible\\n   ```python\\n   import nltk\\n   from nltk.corpus import gutenberg, brown\\n   \\n   # Combine frequencies from both corpora\\n   freq_dist = nltk.FreqDist()\\n   for word in gutenberg.words():\\n       freq_dist[word.lower()] += 1\\n   for word in brown.words():\\n       freq_dist[word.lower()] += 1\\n   ```\\n\\n4. **Generate synthetic frequency norms**: For testing only\\n   ```python\\n   # Assign frequencies based on word length (approximation)\\n   # Short words tend to be more frequent\\n   def approx_frequency(word):\\n       return 1_000_000 / (len(word) ** 2)  # Heuristic\\n   ```\\n\\n**Implementation**: Try SUBTLEX-US download first. If fails, try HuggingFace (Fallbacks 1.1). If all fail, use NLTK corpora (Fallback 1.3) and document the limitation.\\n\\n### Fallback 2: BERT GPU Memory Issues\\n**Problem**: BERT model too large for available GPU memory (especially for RTX A4500 20GB).\\n\\n**Fallback Solutions**:\\n1. **Use smaller BERT variant**: `bert-base-uncased` is 110M parameters, try:\\n   - `distilbert-base-uncased` (66M parameters, ~50% faster)\\n   - `albert-base-v2` (12M parameters, very memory efficient)\\n   - `mobilebert-uncased` (25M parameters)\\n\\n2. **Reduce batch size**: Lower from 16 to 8 or 4\\n   ```python\\n   train_loader = DataLoader(train_dataset, batch_size=4, shuffle=True)  # Reduce batch size\\n   ```\\n\\n3. **Use gradient accumulation**: Simulate larger batch size with smaller memory\\n   ```python\\n   accumulation_steps = 4\\n   optimizer.zero_grad()\\n   for i, batch in enumerate(train_loader):\\n       outputs = model(**batch)\\n       loss = outputs.loss / accumulation_steps  # Normalize\\n       loss.backward()\\n       if (i + 1) % accumulation_steps == 0:\\n           optimizer.step()\\n           optimizer.zero_grad()\\n   ```\\n\\n4. **Use CPU for BERT**: Much slower but will complete\\n   ```python\\n   device = torch.device('cpu')  # Fallback to CPU\\n   ```\\n\\n5. **Skip BERT baseline**: If all else fails, compare only linear models\\n   ```python\\n   # Document that BERT baseline could not be computed due to resource constraints\\n   # Rely on literature comparison with reported BERT performance\\n   ```\\n\\n**Implementation**: Monitor GPU memory. If OOM, switch to distilbert (Fallback 2.1). If still OOM, reduce batch size (Fallback 2.2). Document all fallbacks.\\n\\n### Fallback 3: Bootstrap Too Slow\\n**Problem**: 10,000 bootstrap samples takes too long (> 2 hours).\\n\\n**Fallback Solutions**:\\n1. **Reduce bootstrap samples**: Use 1,000 or 2,000 samples\\n   ```python\\n   n_bootstrap = 2000  # Reduce from 10,000\\n   ```\\n\\n2. **Parallelize bootstrap computation**: Use multiprocessing\\n   ```python\\n   from multiprocessing import Pool\\n   import numpy as np\\n   \\n   def bootstrap_sample(args):\\n       y_true, y_pred1, y_pred2, rng_seed = args\\n       rng = np.random.RandomState(rng_seed)\\n       indices = rng.choice(len(y_true), size=len(y_true), replace=True)\\n       # Compute R\u00b2 difference for this sample\\n       return r2_score(y_true[indices], y_pred2[indices]) - r2_score(y_true[indices], y_pred1[indices])\\n   \\n   with Pool(processes=8) as pool:\\n       args_list = [(y_true, y_pred1, y_pred2, seed) for seed in range(n_bootstrap)]\\n       bootstrap_diffs = pool.map(bootstrap_sample, args_list)\\n   ```\\n\\n3. **Use parametric bootstrap**: Assume normal errors\\n   ```python\\n   # Generate synthetic data from fitted model\\n   # Faster than non-parametric bootstrap\\n   ```\\n\\n4. **Use asymptotic approximation**: Normal approximation for R\u00b2 difference\\n   ```python\\n   # Use formula for variance of R\u00b2 difference\\n   # Less accurate but much faster\\n   ```\\n\\n**Implementation**: Start with 10,000 bootstrap samples. If > 30 minutes, reduce to 2,000 (Fallback 3.1). If still slow, parallelize (Fallback 3.2).\\n\\n### Fallback 4: CMUdict Syllable Counting Too Slow\\n**Problem**: CMUdict lookup for every word in every sentence is slow for 13,129 sentences.\\n\\n**Fallback Solutions**:\\n1. **Pre-cache CMUdict**: Load entire dictionary into memory at start\\n   ```python\\n   import pronouncing\\n   \\n   # Pre-cache all pronunciations\\n   CMUDICT_CACHE = {}\\n   def get_syllables_cached(word):\\n       if word not in CMUDICT_CACHE:\\n           phones = pronouncing.phones_for_word(word)\\n           if phones:\\n               CMUDICT_CACHE[word] = pronouncing.syllable_count(phones[0])\\n           else:\\n               CMUDICT_CACHE[word] = syllables_pkg.estimate(word)  # Fallback\\n       return CMUDICT_CACHE[word]\\n   ```\\n\\n2. **Use syllables package for all words**: Lower accuracy but much faster\\n   ```python\\n   import syllables\\n   syllable_counts = [syllables.estimate(word) for word in words]\\n   ```\\n\\n3. **Sample sentences for evaluation**: Run full evaluation on subset\\n   ```python\\n   # Use 50% sample for testing\\n   sampled_indices = np.random.choice(len(sentences), size=len(sentences)//2, replace=False)\\n   sentences_sampled = [sentences[i] for i in sampled_indices]\\n   ```\\n\\n**Implementation**: Implement caching (Fallback 4.1). If still too slow, use syllables package (Fallback 4.2) and document accuracy trade-off.\\n\\n### Fallback 5: Low OOV Rate for SUBTLEX-US\\n**Problem**: SUBTLEX-US has high OOV rate for domain-specific text (e.g., WeeBIT has children's books, which may have unusual words).\\n\\n**Fallback Solutions**:\\n1. **Backoff to multiple frequency sources**: Combine SUBTLEX-US + Google Books + NLTK\\n   ```python\\n   def get_frequency_hybrid(word, subtlex_dict, google_ngram_dict, nltk_dict):\\n       if word in subtlex_dict:\\n           return subtlex_dict[word]['subtlex_wf']\\n       elif word in google_ngram_dict:\\n           return google_ngram_dict[word]\\n       elif word in nltk_dict:\\n           return nltk_dict[word]\\n       else:\\n           return -1  # OOV\\n   ```\\n\\n2. **Use character-level embedding for OOV words**: More advanced, but better\\n   ```python\\n   # For OOV words, use average frequency of words with similar length\\n   ```\\n\\n3. **Exclude OOV sentences**: Only analyze sentences with 0% OOV rate\\n   ```python\\n   # May introduce bias, but ensures clean evaluation\\n   ```\\n\\n**Implementation**: Compute OOV rate first. If > 20%, implement hybrid approach (Fallback 5.1). Document OOV handling strategy.\\n\\n### Summary of Fallback Priority\\n\\n| Priority | Issue | Fallback | Impact |\\n|----------|-------|----------|--------|\\n| 1 | SUBTLEX-US download | HuggingFace mirror or NLTK | Medium |\\n| 2 | BERT GPU memory | distilbert or CPU | Low (BERT is secondary baseline) |\\n| 3 | Bootstrap slow | Reduce to 2,000 samples | Low (slightly less precise CI) |\\n| 4 | CMUdict slow | Use syllables package | Medium (lower syllable accuracy) |\\n| 5 | High OOV rate | Hybrid frequency sources | Medium (may affect frequency features) |\",\n  \"testing_plan\": \"## TESTING PLAN: Validate Experiment Before Full Execution\\n\\n### Phase1: Mini-Dataset Testing (Expected time: 10 minutes)\\n\\n**Objective**: Verify that all components work on a small subset before running full experiment.\\n\\n```python\\n# 1.1 Test with mini dataset (3 examples)\\ndef test_mini_dataset():\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Test all components on mini dataset (3 examples).\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    # Load mini dataset\\n    mini_path = Path('/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_nOuUUSNqdMp4/3_invention_loop/iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_dataset_1/mini_data_out.json')\\n    with open(mini_path) as f:\\n        mini_data = json.load(f)\\n    \\n    # Extract 3 examples (1 from WeeBIT, 2 from CEFR-SP)\\n    test_examples = [\\n        mini_data['datasets'][0]['examples'][0],  # WeeBIT\\n        mini_data['datasets'][1]['examples'][0],  # CEFR-SP\\n        mini_data['datasets'][1]['examples'][1],  # CEFR-SP\\n    ]\\n    \\n    test_sentences = [ex['input'] for ex in test_examples]\\n    test_scores = [float(ex['output']) for ex in test_examples]\\n    \\n    print(\\\"=== Mini-Dataset Test ===\\\")\\n    print(f\\\"Number of test sentences: {len(test_sentences)}\\\")\\n    print(f\\\"Sentences: {test_sentences}\\\")\\n    print(f\\\"Scores: {test_scores}\\\")\\n    \\n    # Test1: SUBTLEX-US loading (or fallback)\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n--- Test 1: SUBTLEX-US Loading ---\\\")\\n    try:\\n        subtlex_dict = download_subtlex_us()\\n        print(f\\\"\u2713 SUBTLEX-US loaded: {len(subtlex_dict)} words\\\")\\n    except Exception as e:\\n        print(f\\\"\u2717 SUBTLEX-US failed: {e}\\\")\\n        print(\\\"  Using NLTK fallback...\\\")\\n        subtlex_dict = create_nltk_fallback()  # Implement fallback\\n        print(f\\\"\u2713 NLTK fallback loaded: {len(subtlex_dict)} words\\\")\\n    \\n    # Test2: Feature extraction\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n--- Test 2: Feature Extraction ---\\\")\\n    try:\\n        X_mini, feature_names, raw_features = extract_dataset_features(test_sentences, subtlex_dict)\\n        print(f\\\"\u2713 Features extracted: {X_mini.shape}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Feature names: {feature_names}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Sample features: {raw_features[0]}\\\")\\n    except Exception as e:\\n        print(f\\\"\u2717 Feature extraction failed: {e}\\\")\\n        return False\\n    \\n    # Test3: Linear model training\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n--- Test 3: Linear Model ---\\\")\\n    try:\\n        from sklearn.linear_model import Ridge\\n        model = Ridge()\\n        model.fit(X_mini, test_scores)\\n        predictions = model.predict(X_mini)\\n        r2 = r2_score(test_scores, predictions)\\n        print(f\\\"\u2713 Linear model trained: R\u00b2 = {r2:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Predictions: {predictions}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  True scores: {test_scores}\\\")\\n    except Exception as e:\\n        print(f\\\"\u2717 Linear model failed: {e}\\\")\\n        return False\\n    \\n    # Test4: Bootstrap CI (with only 100 samples for speed)\\n    print(\\\"\\\\n--- Test 4: Bootstrap CI (100 samples) ---\\\")\\n    try:\\n        y_pred_dummy1 = test_scores + np.random.normal(0, 0.1, len(test_scores))  # Dummy predictions\\n        y_pred_dummy2 = test_scores + np.random.normal(0, 0.05, len(test_scores))  # Better predictions\\n        \\n        ci_result = compute_bootstrap_ci(\\n            np.array(test_scores), \\n            y_pred_dummy1, \\n            y_pred_dummy2,\\n            n_bootstrap=100  # Small for testing\\n        )\\n        print(f\\\"\u2713 Bootstrap CI computed\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Difference: {ci_result['difference']:.4f}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  95% CI: [{ci_result['ci_lower']:.4f}, {ci_result['ci_upper']:.4f}]\\\")\\n    except Exception as e:\\n        print(f\\\"\u2717 Bootstrap CI failed: {e}\\\")\\n        return False\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\\\\n=== Mini-Dataset Test PASSED ===\\\")\\n    return True\\n```\\n\\n### Phase 2: Component Testing (Expected time: 30 minutes)\\n\\n**Objective**: Test each major component independently with realistic data size.\\n\\n```python\\n# 2.1 Test SUBTLEX-US integration with sample sentences\\n# (Run this AFTER Test 1 passes)\\ndef test_subtlex_integration():\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Test SUBTLEX-US word frequency extraction.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    test_sentences = [\\n        \\\"The cat sat on the mat.\\\",  # Common words\\n        \\\"Antidisestablishmentarianism is a long word.\\\",  # Rare word\\n        \\\"The quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog.\\\"  # Mixed frequency\\n    ]\\n    \\n    subtlex_dict = download_subtlex_us()\\n    \\n    for sent in test_sentences:\\n        freqs, oov_rate = extract_word_frequencies(sent, subtlex_dict)\\n        print(f\\\"Sentence: {sent}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  Frequencies: {freqs}\\\")\\n        print(f\\\"  OOV rate: {oov_rate:.2%}\\\")\\n        \\n        # Check for reasonable values\\n        assert all(f >= -1 for f in freqs), \\\"Frequency should be >= -1 (log scale)\\\"\\n        assert 0 <= oov_rate <= 1, \\\"OOV rate should be between 0 and 1\\\"\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\u2713 SUBTLEX-US integration test PASSED\\\")\\n\\n# 2.2 Test CMUdict syllable counting\\ndef test_syllable_counting():\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Test syllable counting with CMUdict.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    test_words = [\\n        (\\\"cat\\\", 1),\\n        (\\\"computer\\\", 3),\\n        (\\\"antidisestablishmentarianism\\\", 8),\\n        (\\\"the\\\", 1),\\n        (\\\"syllable\\\", 3),\\n    ]\\n    \\n    for word, expected_syllables in test_words:\\n        count, is_oov = count_syllables_cmudict(word)\\n        status = \\\"\u2713\\\" if count == expected_syllables else \\\"\u2717\\\"\\n        print(f\\\"{status} {word}: {count} syllables (expected {expected_syllables})\\\")\\n    \\n    # Test OOV handling\\n    oov_word = \\\"supercalifragilisticexpialidocious\\\"\\n    count, is_oov = count_syllables_cmudict(oov_word)\\n    print(f\\\"OOV word '{ooov_word}': {count} syllables (is_oov={is_oov})\\\")\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\u2713 Syllable counting test PASSED\\\")\\n\\n# 2.3 Test BERT model (small scale)\\ndef test_bert_model():\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Test BERT model training and prediction.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    # Use small subset\\n    test_sentences = [\\\"This is a test sentence.\\\", \\\"Another test sentence here.\\\"] * 10  # 20 samples\\n    test_scores = [0.5, 0.7] * 10\\n    \\n    try:\\n        device = torch.device('cuda' if torch.cuda.is_available() else 'cpu')\\n        tokenizer = BertTokenizer.from_pretrained('bert-base-uncased')\\n        \\n        # Create dataset\\n        dataset = ReadabilityBERTDataset(test_sentences, test_scores, tokenizer)\\n        dataloader = DataLoader(dataset, batch_size=4)\\n        \\n        # Initialize model\\n        model = BERTReadabilityModel()\\n        model.to(device)\\n        \\n        # Test forward pass\\n        batch = next(iter(dataloader))\\n        input_ids = batch['input_ids'].to(device)\\n        attention_mask = batch['attention_mask'].to(device)\\n        \\n        outputs = model(input_ids, attention_mask)\\n        print(f\\\"\u2713 BERT forward pass: output shape = {outputs.shape}\\\")\\n        \\n        # Test training step\\n        criterion = nn.MSELoss()\\n        optimizer = torch.optim.AdamW(model.parameters(), lr=2e-5)\\n        \\n        loss = criterion(outputs, batch['labels'].to(device))\\n        loss.backward()\\n        optimizer.step()\\n        \\n        print(f\\\"\u2713 BERT training step: loss = {loss.item():.4f}\\\")\\n        \\n    except Exception as e:\\n        print(f\\\"\u2717 BERT model test FAILED: {e}\\\")\\n        return False\\n    \\n    print(\\\"\u2713 BERT model test PASSED\\\")\\n    return True\\n```\\n\\n### Phase 3: Medium-Scale Validation (Expected time: 1 hour)\\n\\n**Objective**: Run experiment on 10% of data to validate full pipeline.\\n\\n```python\\n# 3.1 Run pipeline on 10% subsample\\ndef test_medium_scale():\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Test full pipeline on 10% of data.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    \\n    # Load full dataset\\n    dataset_path = Path('/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_nOuUUSNqdMp4/3_invention_loop/iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_dataset_1/full_data_out.json')\\n    with open(dataset_path) as f:\\n        standardized_data = json.load(f)\\n    \\n    weebit_examples = standardized_data['datasets'][0]['examples']\\n    \\n    # Subsample 10%\\n    np.random.seed(42)\\n    subsample_indices = np.random.choice(len(weebit_examples), \\n                                         size=len(weebit_examples)//10, \\n                                         replace=False)\\n    \\n    subsample = [weebit_examples[i] for i in subsample_indices]\\n    \\n    X_text = [ex['input'] for ex in subsample]\\n    y = np.array([float(ex['output']) for ex in subsample])\\n    \\n    print(f\\\"=== Medium-Scale Test: {len(X_text)} sentences ===\\\")\\n    \\n    # Load SUBTLEX-US\\n    subtlex_dict = download_subtlex_us()\\n    \\n    # Extract features\\n    print(\\\"\\\\nExtracting features...\\\")\\n    X, feature_names, _ = extract_dataset_features(X_text, subtlex_dict)\\n    print(f\\\"\u2713 Features extracted: {X.shape}\\\")\\n    \\n    # Evaluate feature sets\\n    print(\\\"\\\\nEvaluating feature sets...\\\")\\n    results = evaluate_feature_sets(X, y, feature_names, n_folds=3, n_bootstrap=1000)  # 3-fold, 1000 bootstrap\\n    \\n    # Print results\\n    print(\\\"\\\\nResults:\\\")\\n    for set_name in ['average', 'uniformity', 'combined']:\\n        print(f\\\"  {set_name}: R\u00b2 = {results[set_name]['r2']:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    #     words = gutenberg.words()\\n        freq_dist = nltk.FreqDist(w.lower() for w in words)\\n        total_words = len(words)\\n        \\n        subtlex_dict = {}\\n        for word, count in
